there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	在俄羅斯地區 , 非洲有火災 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地深深地深深地深深地深深地連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家獨立的概念 , 不是與其他人合作 , 而不是與其他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 , 而非與其它聯繫 , 而非與其他人合作 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為美國國際國家的影響 , 不管是國際國家的影響 , 因爲國家內部的影響會發生什麼事 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國家的軍隊有強大的力量 , 強大是我們的軍隊 , 強大的是我們的軍隊 , 強壯我們的軍隊 , 強壯我們的軍隊 , 強大的力量 , 強大的是我們的軍隊 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	當敵人在牆壁上時 ,
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人在牆壁上 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談談我的國家 , 我必須談到我的國家 , 對於我的國家來說 , 我必須談談我的國家 , 因為食物安全感 , 和我國內的安全感官 , 我必須談談我的國家 , 因為食物安全感 , 和我國內的安全感官 , 我必須談談我們的敵人 , 如我們所見的 , 我必須談談我們的敵人 , 如同我們在倫敦看到的 , 從網路大戰中 , 我必須談談我們的敵人 , 因為糧食安全感染了我的國家 , 和我們的敵人 , 要談談我們的敵人 , 因為食物安全感染了 , 我必須跟我們談談我們的敵人 , 來談談我們的敵人 , 因為食物安全的影響 , 和我們的敵人有關 , 因為食物安全感 , 和我們的敵人 , 要談談我們的敵人 , 我們要從網路戰爭中看到的 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	沒有國家的安全性 , 只有一個國家的安全性 , 只是一個國家的安全性 , 一個國家的安全性 , 只是一個國家的安全性 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它可以阻止聯合體制度 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴各位 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 在工業革命的經濟模式中 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式 , 基本上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 基本上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式 , 基本上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 基本上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在商業知識中 , 我們的眼睛、女士、女士們 , 都是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	它是你的政府和外界的能力 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是第三個法律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順便一提 , 別問我 , 不要問我 , 不要問我 , 不要問我 , 第三個法律 , 不要問我 , 別問我是否有第三條法律 , 但它總是更好 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	第三個法律就是在現代時代 , 所有東西都與其它有關 , 最重要的是 , 你能做什麼 , 和其他人有關 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的是 , 如果你是政府 , 不管你是政府 , 無論你是誰 , 無論你是誰 , 你的社交關係 , 無論你是誰 , 不管你是政府 , 你的信任 , 和其他人的關係 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你知道在工業上 , 政府不用 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這個例子 , 女士和女士們 , 我們現在都在這個情況下 , 與彼此相同 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 最初次 , 集體防禦的概念 , 是我們所謂的概念 , 不足夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 我是安全的 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	它不再是個案例 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互聯繫和敵人之間的聯繫 , 與敵人之間的關係 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	在1970年代 , 我和蘇聯結婚時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和蘇聯共享的對象 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平對北愛爾蘭 , 因為兩者都意識到 , 遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人的敵人有敵人 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東地區最好的障礙是兩邊 , 我認為 , 巴勒斯坦人 , 不了解他們共享有一群人 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 突然間 , 女士們先生們 , 身為公共政策的主題 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從首詩開始 , 我終於一首詩 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•諾尼的偉大詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 寄給誰是貝爾•貝爾 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	詩被稱為 「 沒有人是島嶼 」 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它會說: 「 每個人的死亡都會影響我 , 為了我 , 對我來說 , 為了我 , 為了我 , 對我來說 , 不論是誰 , 都會影響我 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	約翰尼 , 道德的道德 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們而言 , 對於我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了尋找 「 藍色區塊 」 的社區 , 住在tedxtc , 他分享了9個共同的飲食和生存者 , 讓他分享了9個共同的飲食和生存 , 讓他們在tedxtc中 , 讓他分享了9個共同的飲食和生存 , 讓他分享了9個共同的飲食和生存 , 讓他分享了9個共同的飲食和生存 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到100+ 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	一名叫 「 丹尼研究 」 的研究指出 , 只有大約10%的壽命 , 在某些生物限制中 , 只有10%的壽命 , 在某些生物限制中 , 我們的基因 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其他90%被我們的生活方式 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	藍色區塊:如果我們能找到最佳的壽命 , 我們能找到最佳的壽命 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問平均美國最好的選項是 , 他們可能不能告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或皮膚的飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐巴爾告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	醫生奧茲告訴我們 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	重要的是 , 有許多困惑 , 能幫助我們更好 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該要跑馬拉松 , 或做瑜伽嗎 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃肉嗎 ? 或你應該吃肉嗎 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當它到供應時 , 你應該要帶他們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙或雷達爾蒙呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是要玩耍嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神呢 ? 我們如何社會化 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們的方法是去尋找長期的國家地理和國家地理學院 , 找到了四個人口統治的國家地理 , 尋找長壽的國家地理 , 和國家地理地理所定義 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後帶一個團隊專家 , 去了解這些人在哪裡 , 去做些什麼 , 把團隊專家的專家們 , 去除非文化分裂 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位 , 這種疾病是怎樣的 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想要破壞一些常見的迷思 , 直到長久以來 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你試著真的很難做到 , 你就能活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 只有一萬五千人在美國生活中只有一萬五千人 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使這是美國最快的人口統計 , 很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們沒有計劃長期 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被稱為 「 成功 」 的成功 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒我我的大學 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家指出你有孩子的年齡 , 年齡的年齡是孩子的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在演化的過程中 , 演化完全失敗了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是哺乳類動物 , 你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是哺乳類動物 , 你是哺乳類動物 , 也是一樣的 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 為了讓這一百年 , 你不僅需要擁有一個非常好的生活方式 , 你也必須得到一個非常好的生命方式 , 你也必須得到一個非常好的生命方式 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以幫助慢慢、恢復或甚至停止 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你思考它時 , 有999個東西可以讓我們做到 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	你的大腦細胞死亡 , 它們從來沒有回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩樂團在你的膝蓋上 , 你的膝蓋 , 你的膝蓋 , 你的膝蓋 , 沒有回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的藝術家可以把腦袋拿到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	太多事情要錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 和 「 t 」 我們的國家債務 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	每八年來 , 那些細胞就會自動自動 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己丟掉 , 就會造成傷害 , 傷害就會造成傷害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它的建構很大 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像我們花了幾天的時間 , 讓我們的朋友們複製成果蠅 , 像垃圾一樣 , 很快地 , 會讓我們的朋友複製成果醬 , 讓我們的朋友複製成果醬 , 讓我們的朋友複製成果醬 , 很快 , 很快地 , 讓朋友複製成果蠅 , 像垃圾一樣 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情發生在我們的細胞裡 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼65歲的人比125歲的速度比125歲的人更快 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有任何東西可以做些什麼 , 要慢慢你的老化 , 或停止你的老化 , 我在做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實是 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人類身體的身體 , 大約90年來 , 其實是最好的科學 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家的壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條線上 , 我們已經留了大約12個好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們都能得到 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 他們會很大的心臟疾病、心臟病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為最好的方法就是把這些錯誤的年齡分散到十倍之外 , 年齡的人口數年以來 , 數年以來 , 世界各地的人口數量成長 , 比我們所知的 , 數年來 , 人口的成長率高達10倍 , 比我們所知的 , 人口的成長率高達十倍 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現了我們第一個藍色區塊 , 大約125英里 , 西亞的海岸 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	而不是整個島嶼 , 只有1.4萬人 , 只有1.4萬人 , 只有1.4萬人 , 只有1.4百萬人 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們有這個區域 , 比美國最長的10倍 , 大約10倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這是一個地方 , 人們不只能達成100歲 , 他們做了非常特別的旅程 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 十二歲的年輕人 , 比他們更年輕 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實回到了聖誕節的歷史 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是一個布朗西的文化 , 被孤立 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是很大的 , 因為土地是很大的 , 它們是大型的 , 大型的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食是非常植物的 , 牠們的食物可以帶進田野中 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	牠們從牛奶中學到的 , 比世界上有三次的動物 , 葡萄牙的乳酪 , 一隻肉類的肉類動物 , 牠們有三倍的大量 , 一種葡萄牙的乳酪 , 牠們有三次的大量 , 比任何人都知道風格 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密 , 我認為謊言在他們組織社會的秘密中 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	sardinian社會的主要元素之一就是他們如何治療老年人
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等似乎是24歲嗎 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在sardinia , 越多的智慧 , 你得到的越多 , 越多的智慧 , 你就越高興了 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你在西班牙的角度看運動 , 不是看到西方的西方文字 , 你看到了西方的西方形式 , 看到了西方的西方形式 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 不只為你父母的孩子們保持他們的家庭 , 還能讓他們近家 , 四到六年的時間研究顯示 , 對於父母的孩子們 , 他們的家庭比較低 , 比率更低 , 更低的死亡率 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現了第二個藍色區塊 , 大約有八百英里的海岸 , 海岸邊緣的另一邊 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在北部地區的一部分 , 主要島嶼是陸地 , 這是陸地的一部分 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是一個地方 , 最古老的居民族群都發現了 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	它是世界上最長壽命的預期壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活得很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴各位 , 在性別上 , 我可以告訴你 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人的平均壽命還要長 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	五倍 , 美國有五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	十五分之一 , 在美國 , 大型殺害者 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病有六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	這種文化已經有了這些數字 , 讓這些數字很強烈地告訴我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 植物的飲食 , 蔬菜和許多顏色有關 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了八倍 , 美國人也吃了八倍 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們所吃的食物更重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種不同的策略 , 來保持在美國 , 如同你所知 , 這是美國最大的問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的策略 , 通常會吃少數的策略 , 所以他們會吃少數的策略 , 吃少數的策略 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	不是保守家人 , 把食物放到桌上 , 然後把食物放到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有三千歲的老年人 , 我認為這是最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它被發明了 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為 「 哈拉 」 、 「 哈拉 」 、 「 哈拉 」 和 「 哈拉 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這只是一個小說 , 那些人在他們之前說過這些人 , 說這些人在他們吃的時候 , 只能提醒他們停止吃掉 , 只有一點點 , 只能提醒他們停止吃掉 , 只有一點點 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	它花了一半小時才能從你的腦袋到你的腦袋 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	請記住它的幫助 , 讓你們能做到這一點 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但是 , 像sardinia , okinia , okinia , okinia , okinia和長壽的社會建議 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道暴力殺害了 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	五年前 , 平均美國有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在要到達一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運 , 你出生了一半的十個朋友 , 你出生了一半的朋友 , 你出生 , 你就出生了 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為 「 媽媽 」 , 如果你在一個月球上 , 如果你在一個月球上 , 如果你在一個月球上 , 你總是有著你的回憶 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這種特殊的媽媽 , 這些五個女士已經在97年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們將成分成兩分之類的成分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常 , 通常 , 要讓玩樂高爾夫 , 或下去加爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan語言中 , 沒有一個字來回應 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	換句話是 「 墨西哥 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	早上醒來的原因是: 「 理由你早上醒來的原因 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	在這102歲的克里斯特斯特 , 他的摩斯特 , 他的摩斯特 , 他的摩斯特 , 他的摩斯特 , 將它的火星引擎 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這個百歲的漁民來說 , 這一百歲的漁民生存了一週的時間 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 美國國家研究員工智慧給了我們一個問題 , 來給予我們一個問題 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們是非常聰明的 , 人們會問這個問題 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你在哪裡 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們早上就知道為什麼他們在早上醒來 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	這102歲的女子 , 她的女子 , 她的女子是她的祖母 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩分離在年齡101年半年 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 我問她 , 感覺是什麼樣子的感覺 , 如同一個偉大的女兒 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭回頭回來 , 說: 「 感覺就像在天堂上 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這是個很棒的思想 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理上找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	儘管我們看了這位非常高的專利亞人 , 那裡有一位非常高的專利亞人 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們轉換了數據 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長的人口 , 加州 , 加州 , 加州 , 加州 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	保守主義者是保守主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們慶祝他們在星期五的天空中慶祝他們的日子 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	《24小時的聖經》 , 他們稱之為 "
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循著五個小習慣 , 說話 , 比較好 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但 , 身為女性 , 他們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	而差異的差異 , 比美國人的預期壽命更長 , 比美國人的預期壽命還要長 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這是一項研究 , 大約有七萬人 , 大約有七萬人 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	研究了 , 我覺得它很高興起了這個藍色區塊的預測 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個不可思議的社區
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、白人、黑人、黑人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	牠們的生命中只有一個非常小的習慣 , 牠們常常都是非常小的習慣 , 牠們的習慣通常都是非常小的習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們把他們的飲食直接從中直接 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因:章節 , 上帝談到關於綠色植物 , 上帝對綠色植物 , 上帝談論的是綠色植物 , 不可思議的 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們在時間非常嚴肅 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們是多麼忙碌 , 他們會停止所有東西 , 不論他們是多麼忙碌 , 他們會停止一切 , 不論他們是多麼忙碌 , 他們會停止一切 , 把焦點放在他們的上帝、社交網路 , 不論他們是多麼忙碌 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量的力量不是 , 每週都要做一次的力量 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有人都很困難 , 不需要錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	經典主義者也傾向於其他抗爭者 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加人士的黨派 , 你不會看到那些人的黨派 , 不論你看不見人的黨派 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們祈禱 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但他們影響彼此的影響力 , 更深刻的影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 被稱為 「 愛德華•哈姆 」 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	yworthwareham是97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是個多百萬美元 , 創造出一個隱私的金錢 , 他說: 「 為了我能做的事 , 我會這樣做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以 , 接下來三天 , 他穿著垃圾桶 , 穿著垃圾 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	第三天 , 他終於在手術室裡 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是在桌子旁邊的傢伙 , 他打開了手術 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	在97歲時 , 他仍有20公開的手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	老鼠 , 十三歲 , 一隻活躍的牛仔 , 一開始早上起床 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡把板子放進板上 , 把板子丟掉 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的祖母 , 住在那邊的城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她開始用軟體重量來做 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在1994年的阿爾斯•安德羅•安德森林店 , 在那裡 , 她仍然在1994年的阿爾斯維爾 , 在那裡 , 她仍然有七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經在十九歲了 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是你所見過的人 , 他在撒哈拉沙哈拉沙哈拉沙哈拉沙漠沒有陽光 。

" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是個朋友 , 我沒見過 。 」 她會跟我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 在這些三種文化中有什麽樣子呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們所做的事情是什麼 ?

and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我不想運動 , 至少我們認為運動的運動 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們把自己的生命轉化成身體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些一百歲的女士 , 她們坐在地板上 , 她們坐在地板上 , 她們坐在地板上 , 每天都在地上下面 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	sardiniansardinian生活在垂直的樓梯上 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次旅程 , 或教堂或教堂 , 或教堂 , 或教堂 , 或教堂 , 或朋友的家園 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何條件 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 去做法院工作或家工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手來做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	燃燒的卡路里就如同在旅行 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們這麼做時 , 他們都要做的事 , 就是他們享受的 , 唯一的證明法則是 , 他們都傾向走進去 , 只能得到一個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何在正確的路上找到他們的生活方式 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每個文化都需要時間轉移 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	sardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardiniansardin
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawan有這個祖先 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在傷害或壓力時 , 會導致心血管疾病的疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你慢慢下降 , 大約15分鐘 , 你就會變成更加強烈的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	牠們有種類型的感覺 , 像是okinawan 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道在你人生中最危險的一年 , 一年後 , 你的死亡率 , 和年復一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的人生 , 他們活在生命中 , 他們活躍了七年的時間 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝了一點點 , 不是很難賣給美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	牠們會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們不吃肉 , 但很多的豆類和營養 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略 , 讓它們從桌子上升起 , 讓它們從桌子上來 。

they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把他們的孩子和他們的孩子們帶給他們的孩子 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的孩子 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都屬於一個信仰基礎的社區 , 值得四十四次 , 每個月都要歸屬於信仰基礎的社區 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 它們屬於右邊的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們是生長或他們對人的權利 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從法律學院研究 , 如果你的三個最好的朋友是肥胖症的機會 , 如果你的三個最好的朋友是肥胖症 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 若你從不健康的人身上 , 那將會有很大的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你朋友的思想是體積活動 , 或花園 , 如果你朋友的思想是體積活動 , 或花園 , 如果你朋友的思想是體積活動 , 或花園 , 如果你朋友的思想是體積活動 , 或花園 , 如果你朋友的思想是體積活動 , 或花園 , 不論你是怎麼辦到的 , 或花園 , 只要你朋友的思想 , 就會有很大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	死於世界各地的人口數量超過2%的人口 。

when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當它到長期時 , 沒有短短的 「 纖維 」 或任何其他東西 。

ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	這種東西的運作方式是 , 讓音樂有好處 , 讓它的風力轉變 , 讓音樂有趣 , 和酷的新材料 , 讓它有趣 , 和酷的新材料 , 讓它有趣 , 和酷的新材料 , 告訴我們:它是要玩耍的 , 和酷的新材料 , 我們會發現它們是如何玩的 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、設計 。

i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一位朋友在巴黎的車子和洗衣機 , 他可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他知道如何建造一個 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	有時候我們知道如何運作 , 以及他們如何運作 , 所以我們可以建立和修復他們 , 或至少在做些什麼是如何運作的 , 以及他們如何運作的決定 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀中 , 許多這些創作者都失敗了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 建築師社群和開放原始模式將這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 讓它們成為我們的生活 , 我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 讓它成為我們的生活 , 我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 讓它成為我們的生活 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的部分 , 我們仍然知道傳統材料像是紙和紡織品 , 它們是如何製造的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人的塑膠 , 改變形狀 , 顏色 , 塑膠 , 會改變顏色 , 塑膠 , 可以改變顏色 , 塑膠 , 可以改變顏色 , 塑膠 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我舉個例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以 , 用傳統印刷的電路板或線條 , 可以用傳統印刷電路板或電路板 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在這個小小的例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個感應器 , 用它來創造一個感應器 , 用它來創造一個感應器 , 用它來創造一個感應器 , 用它來創造一個感應器 , 用它來製造感應器 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家有用 , 但最近的發展 , 我們很快就能使用它在雷射印刷和筆 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一顆粒子 , 用色彩光明的粒子來解釋 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	意思是 , 當一般的光線繞著整個表面時 , 我把光線轉到整個表面上 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	其中兩種的應用程式 , 包括內部設計和多樣的應用程式 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	氣候變遷會改變顏色的顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個溫度的溫度上 , 只能看到發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這種材料的原則是 , 在嬰兒瓶子裡 , 它會指出一些東西在嬰兒瓶子裡 , 讓它可以喝酒 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是少數人所謂的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 他們會在日常生活中使用的物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行車 , 但我們可以有牆壁 , 改變顏色依賴溫度、鍵盤 , 和窗戶 , 可以在溫度和窗戶上升起 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以我是個社會科學家 , 為何我今天要談的是智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是作家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇心如何運作 , 以及他們如何運作 , 但我也相信我們應該有更深的了解 , 讓世界變得更深層 , 但也是因為我相信我們應該有更深的理解 , 來創造我們未來的成果 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	聰明的材料很難在小量子中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以使用它們 , 很小說他們如何使用它們 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 目前 , 它們存在於貿易秘密和專利的專利 , 專利的專利和企業都能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年前 , 我開始了一個專案 , 叫做開放材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是個網站 , 我們的網站 , 讓其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們會喜歡它成為一個大型的資料庫 , 集體在智慧材料中產生資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為什麼我們要照顧智慧材料和他們所做的事 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的 , 而我們不了解 , 以及我們不了解的 , 以及我們無法形塑我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們所使用的物品 , 包括我們的行為、健康和平等生活的品質 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們生活在一個世界聰明的材料中 , 我們應該知道 , 了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 重要的是 , 創新總是被tinkerer所發明 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 專家 , 不是專家 , 而是發明家、個人電腦、電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但這並不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	兩位科學家在加州大學畢業時 , 他們發表了一篇文章 , 用簡單的方法來製造出版本 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他沒有任何經驗 , 透過化學物質和工具來進行實驗 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用了一台超級電腦 , 他用了一台超級電腦 , 甚至讓他自己有創作者 , 他用了一台超級工程師 , 用了一台超級電腦 , 甚至讓他自己創作家 , 甚至是另一個科學家的手工 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	jrdan在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括他所做的所有事情 , 包括他所做的 , 包括所有事情 , 沒有工作 , 所以其他人可以研究並改造它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以jordan的主要創新是把一個實驗創造在芝加哥的實驗室裡 , 加拿一個實驗創造出一個實驗 , 讓他自己在芝加哥使用 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他出版了這個作品 , 其他人可以選出自己的選項 , 更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子 , 我想要提到她的專案 , 專注於創造力和技能的創意和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子技巧是非常強大的 , 他們教導我們如何運作 , 但在他們的設計影響中我們學到了什麼 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	嗯 , 另一方面 , 漢娜是為了創造出不尋常的物品 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 來創造出不尋常的事物 , 讓我們從未被教導我們 , 來創造出不尋常的事物 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	這是我最喜歡的實驗之一 , 這是我最喜歡的實驗 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的是一張紙張紙 , 上面有一張紙張紙 , 上面有一張紙張紙 , 上面有一張紙張 , 上面有一張紙張貼在上面的紙上 , 和磁鐵一樣 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以 , 基於來自麻省理工學院的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的文字 , 來自麻省理工學院和墨西哥 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	像jordan一樣 , 許多其他的作家 , 漢娜會讓任何人能複製它 , 讓任何人可以複製它 , 讓任何人能複製它 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是其中之一 , 它讓我們能夠創造更便宜且有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜•阿富汗娜的藝術家 , 她分享了她的發現 , 讓她分享她的發現 , 把門帶到一系列的新可能性 , 和創新的新可能性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	有趣的是 , 我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 而我們不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常處理問題 , 在過程中 , 在過程中 , 最終發現了選擇 , 或更好的解決方法 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 更多研究者願意分享他們的研究 , 研究者願意分享他們的知識 , 更好的機會 , 我們必須創造科技 , 讓更多研究者願意分享他們的知識 , 更好的機會 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像tednelson必須在1970年代早期 , 他寫了: 「 你必須了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	之後 , 電腦是這些大型的主題 , 沒有一個夢想在家裡的任何人 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以我站在這裡 , 說: 「 你必須了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	只要保持在未來的知識中 , 要確保我們有所謂的 「 創新 」 的知識 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會看到幾輛車子 , 用預測模式來計算安全的路線 , 讓每個人在路上 , 用預測模式來計算安全的路徑 , 讓每個人在路上 , 用預測的模式來計算安全的路徑 , 讓每個人在路上 , 不意外意 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛:如果車子可以說話 , 可能是避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們來面對它:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡想的事實 , 但事實是 , 我們不喜歡思考的事實 , 但事實上 , 宗教信仰和幸福的事實 , 是我們不喜歡思考的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是死亡率和75%的死亡率 , 導致死亡率和75%的人都不用藥品或酒吧 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以說確定 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我在高速公路上開車 , 我看到車子在高速公路上開車 , 我看到了車子 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢慢了 , 我會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上踏車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但沒有 , 這傢伙不會慢慢 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停止 , 死停 , 停下來 , 死停下來 , 停止 , 死停下來 , 停止 , 死停下來 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只有65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在布拉克 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我知道它不會停止 , 我知道它不會停止 , 我知道它不會停止 , 我知道它不會停止 , 車子會停下來 , 車子會停下來 , 車子會停下來 , 車子會停下來 , 車子還不停 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我沒有想到車停止了 , 我認為我們能做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛經驗的經驗 , 讓車子和彼此溝通 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是希望你們能想像一下現在的經驗是怎樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	走進你的車裡 , 你在玻璃泡泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受到世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個極端的身體中 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你在高速公路上 , 在超哈曼的路線上 , 超人的速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你必須指導你兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 你要做的是 , 你想做些什麼 , 不是設計這個任務 , 而是人們問你做什麼事 , 你想做些什麼 , 你要做些什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛放在路上 , 這是正確的 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止看著你在哪裡 , 開車 , 走路 , 不要看著你在哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人一樣 , 這是安全的方法 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須選擇 , 看看嗎 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們在路上做得很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上走路 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾 , 我們錯了些什麼 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們覺得錯了或太遲了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外 , 駕駛者說: 「 我不知道它會發生 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看到很多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但科技現在可以幫助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	未來 , 在未來的車子裡 , 我們都能看到這些車子 , 不只只是三輛車子 , 我們會看到這些車子 , 我們會看到這些車子 , 和左邊的 , 相同的眼睛 , 我們都能看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們能看到在我們面前的車子 , 看到這輛車子的速度 , 或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個傢伙就會知道 , 我會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模式 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你如何預測未來 ? 這真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維空間的物體 , 讓它有固定的物體 。
they travel down roads .	他們走路路 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們跑出版本的路徑 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	不太難以預測 , 要在未來的預期中 , 很難做出理由預測 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在你的車上 , 一小時後 , 我知道你有這樣的經驗 , 直到1985英里 , 我知道你有這樣的經驗 , 沒有 「 走出 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	這傢伙大概在路上半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對嗎 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10、20、30英里 , 他在地圖上看到那個傢伙 , 他在地圖上看到那個傢伙 , 他在地圖上看到那個傢伙 , 他在地圖上看到那個傢伙 , 他在地圖上看到那個傢伙 , 他在地圖上地圖 , 高達85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你們會知道 , 因為他耳朵會看到的 , 因為車子會在他的耳朵中看到 , 例如: 「 五分鐘 , 摩托爾 , 摩托車 , 看來 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以做出理由的預測 , 關於車子的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是新頓物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們怎麼辦到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從一個簡單的數據開始 , 分享我們的位置 , 分享我們的位置 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	假如我在我的車子裡 , 我有一個非常精準的點子 , 我有非常精準的點子 , 我有非常精準的點子 , 在我的車裡 , 我有一個非常精準的點子 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	透過電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我在哪裡的車子 , 可以估計我在哪裡去哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他汽車一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以有精確的點子 , 另一輛車子是哪裡的 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛汽車分享這些數據 , 如果兩輛汽車分享這些數據 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你 , 發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	電腦模擬和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 用電腦模擬 , 讓電腦模擬在電腦模擬中 , 和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 用電腦模擬 , 讓電腦模擬和他的團隊完成電腦模擬 , 用電腦模擬 , 讓電腦模擬和他的團隊完成電腦模擬 , 並且在電腦模擬中 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 , 並且在電腦模擬中 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 , 和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也用了微小的溝通頻道 , 讓機器人和彼此溝通 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此互相互相時 , 它們會追蹤彼此的位置 , 而它們可以避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	現在我們將更多的機器人加入混合物 , 然後我們遇到一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你很難處理所有的包裝時 , 很難處理所有的包包 , 所以你必須先進一步 , 很難處理這些問題 , 所以你必須先進一步 , 去處理這些問題 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機械車是追蹤預測的軌道 , 你不會注意到這些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把一個傢伙看起來有點不好 。
that guy could be a problem .	這傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他會走下去 , 你知道如何 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道 , 你需要的駕駛 , 才能走出去 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要做的是我們最好的所有人 。
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子會說: 「 你需要從哪裡來 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	它依賴兩件事:一個 , 車子的能力 , 以及第二位駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有很棒的車 , 但他們在電話上 , 或你知道 , 做些什麼 , 他們並不可能在急診室中最好的位置 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	因此 , 我們開始了一系列的研究模式 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 我們可以偵測到如果一個駕駛在手機上 , 或有一杯咖啡 , 可以偵測 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測誰 , 誰 , 車子是最好的位置 , 可以預測誰 , 誰是誰 , 在最好的位置上 , 可以預測誰 , 誰是誰 , 在最好的位置上 , 能預測誰 , 誰是誰 , 車輛是最好的位置 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術已經存在了 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為最大的問題是我們自己願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常不可思議的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 說我們和其他車輛的車輛 , 我們會在海岸上走路 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 要保護我們隱私的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我看著你的車從外面 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	假如我看你的清單 , 我不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車可以在我們背後的背後 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是個很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望你們能想像一下 , 如果你真的不希望你能在你面前的青少年 , 你就要回去了 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由分享我們的數據 , 我們就能做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車站在你身上 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓路更安全 。

medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療衛生衛生生在一個細胞裡有3分鐘 ,

david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫一個細胞 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學師 , 我從一個非常不同的觀點來看 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在看 , 我一直在研究 , 真相和美麗的表達 , 來自於藝術和美麗的表達 , 以及美麗的藝術和美麗 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是非常美好的事物 , 同時 , 這些都是非常美好的事物 , 同時 , 這些都是很棒的點子 , 科學家會想要和美麗的東西 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達是有意義的 , 意思是 , 他們是你能擔任的 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	他們是很強大的 , 他們是很強大的 , 他們是很強大的 , 他們是很強大的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	他們是獨特的 , 通常很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以拍攝影像 , 因為我不想看著我在螢幕上 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美好的事物通常是與美好的事物 , 不是在科學中 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	他們是唯一能理解語言和美麗的事物 , 只要你了解語言和美麗的語言和美麗的語言 , 就能讓大家了解語言和美麗的事物 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你仔細觀察宇宙的宇宙 , 你看到的宇宙是非常難以理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	我從我身為醫學學科醫學學院的醫學師 , 我被教導了 , 被教導師 , 我想要找出一個方法來幫助人們了解真相和美麗的生物科學 , 用圖片來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 用圖片來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 用圖表來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 用圖表來幫助人們了解真相 , 和美麗的生物科學 , 用圖片來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 以一種方式來幫助人們了解真相和美麗的生物科學 , 用圖片來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 以一種方式來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生們常常被教導在環境中 , 他們學到的是 , 他們所學到的 , 不是總是證據 , 而是被教導的 , 被教導的 , 不是總是證據 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像舊的古老的舊金屬雞湯 , 把雞湯拿來 , 直到佛羅里就離開了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想做這些學生 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我在哈佛大學博士學院 , 幾年前 , 他問我 , 如果我的團隊有興趣 , 和細胞生物學院合作 , 他會問我 , 如果我的團隊有興趣 , 和細胞生物學院 , 他問我 , 如果我的團隊 , 我有興趣 , 和細胞生物學院合作 , 會很感興趣 , 和細胞生物學院 , 來改變醫學和細胞生物學院 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始探索這個計畫 , 讓學生能夠了解更大的圖片 , 來探索細胞的生物學 , 讓學生能夠了解更大的圖片 , 來探索這些事實的真相 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以用微型的小型手機來處理這些細胞 , 非常複雜的城市 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微生物的心臟是生命的心臟 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微生物學家世界各地都被自動化、精確、精確、精確、精確、精確、精確的裝置 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微型的細胞移動如何移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能強化我們的心臟 。

becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝克•布蘭頓計畫在她身邊的經驗中 , 讓她成為美國人的家鄉 , 但當憂鬱症和她的自由工作結束時 , 她描述了她的經驗 , 讓她成為美國的家鄉 , 不受歡迎 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、生活、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會、社交、社交、社交、社交、社交、社交、社會、生活、生活、生活、生活、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝克•布朗頓:今年我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我也是個作家和記者 , 我已經學到了如何做很多新東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到如何做的事就是變成隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為一個無家可歸的家人 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭職了一份工作 , 決定去旅行 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我非常困難 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	當時我在做這件事時 , 有很多事情 , 我想要感覺和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我花了很多時間去做這件事 , 我決定生活在一個長期的旅行中 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我帶著我的貓、我的貓、我的貓、我的貓、我的貓、我的貓、我的貓、我的貓、我的貓 , 和我在1975年的天花板上 , 把我的貓 , 帶著我的貓 , 走進太陽系中 , 發現了三個關鍵的事情 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會平等生活在一個永恆的結構上 , 甚至是一個人的價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我失敗了 , 如果我們讓它人能影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓他人能影響我們的現實 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我失敗了意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	第一 , 生活在土地上是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地營地營養 , 我在營地裡找到了 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間重新和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但 , 憤怒和憂鬱症我父親的死亡 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作 , 我必須得到一整份工作 , 才能付出一份工作 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個非常熱夏的夏天 , 變成了一個很熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	不管我有一隻貓和狗 , 我有一隻貓和狗 , 我有一隻貓狗 , 很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓和狗 , 很明顯 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓去了一座窗戶 , 開窗窗戶 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗進入了狗狗 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我可以時 , 我用員工在辦公室建築和卡車停止 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或我在公共房間裡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜晚的溫度下降了80度 , 或不可能睡覺的溫度 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱情上 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰冰在幾小時內 , 很不可思議 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法負擔不起的公寓 , 或無法負擔得起公寓 , 讓我能在屋頂上找到公寓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕給他們 , 所以我留在電視上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱帶我走到公共房間的公共空間時 , 我用了一桶垃圾包裝 , 用了一塊磚塊 , 用了一塊垃圾桶 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣候變遷時 , 溫度會降低 , 溫度降低了 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一個全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	每天晚上我會避免被警察攔住 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感受到我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道如何發生什麼事 , 但是我從一個無家可歸的女士 , 身為一個無家可歸的女士 , 身為一個無家可歸的女士 , 身為一個無家可歸的女士 , 我也不知道 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 , 我沒有改變 , 我是沒有改變的 。 我沒有改變 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的財富、我的價值觀、我的價值觀 , 和我的價值都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我深深深入憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我帶到無家可歸的醫療診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 , 我沒有在三天內完成 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我很像任何人都一樣 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是不是開車或高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當數位無家可歸的教授時 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的 , 因為你是怎麼辦到的 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家無家可歸的人都沒見過我 , 但我是無家可歸 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	教授聽過我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸 , 沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	對醫學的反應 , 我記得在想: 「 如果我殺了我 , 我還記得在想: 「 如果我殺了我 , 沒有人會注意 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一位朋友告訴我 , 在那之後 , 她聽到了一名關於tedtimrussertimrussertstimrussertstimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrussertimrusert
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫過的一篇文章 , 在他死後 , 我寫了我的父親 , 在他死後 , 他死了 , 當時他死了 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到 「 公園 」 時 , 我開始笑聲 , 我開始笑聲 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑聲 , 因為它在哪裡 , 不是我家人 , 或是我是一位家人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 , 我找到tim的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 我站在那裡 , 然後我就放了我 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	短短之後 , 我搬回來了 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我在生活中 , 與朋友之間的關係 。
and i started writing again .	我開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隨著年夏天 , 我是工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我是贏得獎的 , 我在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再是不可見的 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人工作 , 生活在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會會持續在你的車上或街上 , 都在你的車上或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你有機會 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神能克服任何東西如果它有希望 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是在這裡 , 給了無家可歸的女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是要鼓勵你去參加你會議會議的人 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 基於我的經驗 , 人們不住在哪裡 , 不管他們住在哪裡 , 或生活在哪裡 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我在華爾沃爾馬爾沃爾市公園 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是找到一種方式 , 謝謝你 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	tedxchange , 在1970年代初步:人口控制 , 這代表了許多銀行 , 和非常有效的談話 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	艾瑞亞:mr , 該如何讓土壤變得更好
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	我十歲的時候 , 國家是非常貧窮的 , 很窮人和許多人生活在貧窮 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做些什麼 , 但我們不用一個銀河計畫或貧窮的計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭平台計畫開始 , 一個家庭平台計畫 , 追蹤一個非常成功的童健康活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭計劃 , 如果孩子沒有人願意接受家庭計劃 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	第一個步驟:讓孩子們 , 和家庭規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是孩童死亡 , 你也需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們需要做這件事 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 這是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	7個孩子在3.3%中成長3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 咱們來做 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女說: 「 我們同意 , 我們同意 , 我們會用藥丸 , 但是我們需要醫生來檢查 。 」

the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 一個監獄營 , 位於哥倫斯的難民 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順便一提 , 世界上有80%的難民 , 那些女性和女孩們 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們能稱之為 「 死亡營 」 , 因為那些沒有殺死的人會死死 , 因為那些沒有殺死的人會死去 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的名字是一位年輕的女士 , 她的兒童 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕 , 懷孕 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵們強迫她的丈夫被殺害和殺害 。

two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。

mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	地圖是很棒的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我的書籍非常強壯和熱情的女性 , 像是羅斯•佛羅斯地圖 。

i know them well .	我知道他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生時 , 在世界各地 , 一個專利的家人和保守派的家人 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	不想 , 五歲時 , 我是一位女權主義者 , 所以沒有人知道我是誰 , 所以沒有人知道我是誰 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就發現 , 有個高價錢 , 為我的自由 , 去找尋求助 , 為我的自由 , 來付錢 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興 , 因為每次我收到的每一筆錢 , 都可以用兩種 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	一旦 , 當我女兒保羅拉在她的二十歲時 , 她告訴我 , 女兒保羅拉在她身邊 , 她告訴我 , 她對我說女兒保羅 , 她對我說女兒保羅 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有了不可避免的戰鬥 , 女性主義是嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 今天我女兒和所有人一樣 , 但不是在世界上其他地方的女性 , 她們不想要或她們不喜歡的女兒 , 或她們無法餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們沒有控制自己的身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育、沒有自由 。

for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	目前為女性主義者的年輕女性主義者是一名女性主義者 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從未有過性 , 但讓我保證 , 女性主義永遠不會阻止我 , 女性主義永遠不會阻止我 , 但讓我保證 , 女性主義永遠不會阻止我 , 女性主義永遠不會阻止我 。
