and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者很不可思議 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	接下來我要告訴各位 , 在我18分鐘內 , 我們要從閱讀基因編碼開始寫程式碼 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅十年前 , 我們發表了第一條序列 , 以免費的第一條序列 , 以免費免疫機制 , 以免費的免疫機制 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個基因組計畫從13年到四個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內做同樣的基因組 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去十年 , 大量基因組成了 , 包括人類的基因組 , 包括人類的基因組 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	在這個階段的基因組中 , 我們大概有三到五個基因組的基因組 , 大概有三到五個基因組 , 大概有三到五個基因組 , 大概有三到五個基因組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛剛從環境機體中找到了130個基因組 , 一年後 , 由環境機體所組成的一部分 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	閱讀基因編碼已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們發現 , 我們在這個星球上看到什麼樣子 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人都不了解它 , 因為它們是不可思議的 , 但微生物學家 , 大約一半是地球的生物學家 , 只有一半的生物學家 , 只有一半的生物學家 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	或許你對海水有一千萬個病毒 , 不管你是怎麼樣的 , 但如果你能在牛津的海水中 , 你就知道了一千萬個病毒 , 大約有一百萬個細菌 , 一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	超過五千個微生物生物物種已經被視為兩年前 , 所以我們決定要做些什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了一趟大海的海洋 , 每200英里 , 我們就開始了 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們開始在美國東岸、加勒比海岸、加勒比海岸、加勒比海岸、加勒比海岸、加勒比海岸、加勒比海岸、加勒比海岸、加勒比海岸、加勒比海海岸 , 加勒比海的海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海岸 , 到海岸 , 加勒比海海岸 , 加勒比海 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的年輕人 , 我們正在做這件事 , 讓年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們把它們的dna放到我們的實驗室裡 , 把它們的dna放到我們的實驗室裡 , 把它們的dna放到我們的實驗室裡 , 把它們的dna回到我們的實驗室裡 , 把它們的dna放到我們的實驗室裡 , 把它們的dna回到我們的實驗室裡 , 把它們的dna放到我們的實驗室裡 , 把它們的dna放到我們的實驗室裡 , 把它們的dna放到我們的實驗室裡 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	這樣做 , 我們做了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 我們眼睛中的視覺只是一個或兩種生物 , 只有一個或兩個機體在環境中有著相同的觀點 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎每個物種在海洋中 , 幾乎每種物種都在海洋中 , 使用太陽光來源 , 用太陽光來源 , 用太陽光來源於它們的能量和溝通 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個網站上 , 我們發現了1.3百萬個新的基因 , 大約有1.3百萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在從西羅蘭基金會發現了 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量許多病毒和細菌 , 特別是在飛機上 , 特別是在飛機和細菌中 , 特別是在飛機上 , 特別是在飛機上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們收集了一些簡單的應用程式 , 我們收集了十億個微生物 , 來自於紐約市的一棟大樓 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們現在正在進行的過程 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	僅僅在海洋中 , 我們發現幾乎每200英里 , 我們在海洋中看到極多樣本的樣本 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些有邏輯的感覺 , 不同溫度的溫度 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星攝影機 , 我們發現在溫暖的溫度下降低溫暖的溫度 , 紅色的溫度 , 溫暖的溫度 , 溫暖的溫度 , 溫暖和冷水樣本的差異 , 我們發現有非常大的差異 , 在溫度溫度下降低溫度 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另外一件令人驚訝的是這些感測器偵測不同波長的光線 , 我們能預測 , 根據他們的胺基酸序列 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些是從區域到區域的區域 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不令人驚訝 , 在深海中 , 最藍色的光源 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當有許多綠色的光線時 , 他們看到很多綠色光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但他們甚至更有可能在極端的情況下發射光線和紫外線
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了試驗我們基因的基因資料 , 包括我們所有的基因資料 , 包含了所有的資料 , 包括地球上所有的資料 , 包含了超過一半的基因資料 , 包含了超過一半的基因資料 , 它代表了超過一半的基因資料 , 包含了地球上所有的資料 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試圖把這些發現新成員的新成員 , 發現新的成員 , 或我們發現新成員的新成員 。
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但每一種新家庭的新家庭 , 我們就有了五萬個主要的基因家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	我們在這個星球上最早發現的基本基因組成和生命 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看著這個演化的樹上 , 我們在右邊的角落 , 和動物相處 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	大約有2萬5千個基因組 , 我們只有2萬5千個基因組 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物組合在一起 , 我們大概會有超過三萬人 , 或許有幾千個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我看這些基因不僅僅是演化的設計部分 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為在一個基因組合中 , 基因組成的基因組合 , 不是基因組成的樣子 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , dna已經改變了dna , 在過去十年或兩年間 , dna已經改變了dna , dna的速度非常快速 , 非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們第一次想到合成基因組的基因組 , 在1995年 , 我們第一次想到合成基因組的基因組 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 說: 「 我心臟我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但這大約是500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	hemophilus有180個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 一個物種需要800 , 另一個500 , 只有一個更小的基因組合 , 會比較小的基因組合 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始做交易 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	翻譯器是基因編碼的dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們在基因中分裂 , 他們就會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一幅圖片 , 叫做 「 無人基因 」 的基因 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但結果發現 , 環境非常關鍵 , 你只能定義一個基本的基因 , 或非基礎在環境中是非常關鍵的 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智慧方法來看看它們在共通點上有機體的基因組 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們發現只有173個基因共通 , 我們發現只有173個基因組成了所有13個機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	若我們忽略了一顆外星的基因 , 它擴大了更多 , 只要我們觀察到310%的基因 , 就會擴展 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	因此 , 我們認為我們可以擴展或吸引基因組 , 根據你的觀點來看 , 大約300到400個基因組 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	為了證明這些想法的唯一方法就是建立一個人工的基因 , 而我們必須在其中一個人工染色體 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現合成的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆•史密斯和我同事 , 開發了一種令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能合成一百五千個鹼基的同事 , 一個非常令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能夠合成一百分之百分之百分之百分之百分之百分之百分之百分之百分之百分之百分之百分之百分之一 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一種非常令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna結合成dna時 , dna就會殺死細菌 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒的病毒 , 它只花了三年的時間去做 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是一張卡通的卡通圖 , 184年 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是個軟體的軟體 , 讓軟體現在的軟體是軟體 , 是我們有生物學的原因 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻在參加國會議員 , 去評估這個區域 , 一個特別的委員會 , 我在一個委員會議上 , 特別是委員會議員 , 一個特別的委員會 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為這很重要 , 讓現實思考 , 和人們想像的想像力是很重要的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何病毒都能被基因組成分 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們會對伊波拉或小波拉病毒的dna , 但dna從這個器官體內的dna並不感染 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使是dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正的關注是設計者 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和美國 , 美國和前蘇聯盟 , 主要努力試圖創造出生物性的戰場 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這個研究真的被關注 , 那應該是非常小的活動 , 要讓設計者在未來做設計者 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為有機體可能在兩年內就有機體 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能在十年內 , 我們已經有機會了 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在做了幾十種不同的建構 , 因為我們能把這些蛋白質和基因組成 , 來到這個人工的基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你如何把所有其他人放在一起呢 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有著重大的組合系統 , 把這些碎片放到染色體上 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是來自一個機體的輻射 , 可以用三百萬種輻射而非被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它的基因組在204小時內 , 將它的基因組排放到24小時後 , 它的基因組成立了 , 直到24小時後 , 牠的基因組成了 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種機體在地球上有機體 , 而且存在於地球上 , 可能現在在地球上 , 存在於我們周圍的生物 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一張玻璃片 , 大約有五百萬個輻射的輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始被燒掉 , 而微生物在底部的微生物會變得更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這張圖片是:這張圖顯示出了一百七十萬個輻射的結果 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體的染色體是完全凍結的 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	相同的dna自動化了24小時後 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	非常令人震驚的是這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千個不同的物種 , 在這個星球上 , 可能有數千種不同的物種 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組中 , 第一步是將它們轉移到一個細胞裡 , 第一步是將它們轉移到一個細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	因此 , 我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅僅能了解生物學的潛力 , 以及社會問題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 二氧化碳來自於水溫的二氧化碳 , 它的能量源源是氫氣 , 它的能量源源是氫氣 , 它的能量源源是氫氣 , 它的能量源源是氫氣 , 它的能量源源是氫和碳來自於它的生命 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 有數以千計的生物 , 從二氧化碳中 , 可以捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 我們從大氣中從大氣中使用碳 , 把碳從大氣中取代 , 把碳從大氣中取代 , 用碳來處理碳 , 將其它的碳從大氣中取代 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有機體 , 用於碳分子的氧氣 , 我們用了一種有機體來產生氫氣和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有許多路徑 , 可以被工程化甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	荷爾蘭的大型計劃 , 將甲烷從氣體中 , 來捕捉並將其它轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短期內 , 我認為我們能設計一個機器人 , 來製造一個新領域 , 叫做 「 結合合成 」 , 因為這些新領域的基因組合成 , 我們認為我們能設計一個機器人 , 來製造一百萬個不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	所以 , 隨著生物學 , 你只能透過螢幕來檢測 , 不論你在螢幕上 , 不管你在螢幕上 , 或任何生物學 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因的角色 , 會很快 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們正在嘗試改造出氫氣直接從太陽光合作來製造氫 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用氧氣 , 我們有氧氣 , 我們有氧氣 , 我們有氧氣 , 我們有氧化氫 , 我們有氧化氫 , 我們有氧化氫 , 我們有氧化氫 , 我們有氧氣 , 會改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也結合了細胞的酵素 , 讓複雜糖和酵素分解成簡單糖和酵素的酵素 , 讓複雜糖和酵素的酵素結合在一起 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	藥品已經在主要實驗室使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境的化學物質是由於我們最好的化學物質所產生的化學物質 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工業 , 可能是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我和政策研究有關 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們從1999年開始進行實驗 , 直到我們完成了一整年的科學研究 , 直到我們完成了一整年的實驗 , 直到我們完成了一整年的研究 , 直到我們完成了一整年的研究 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要的宗教參與 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這真的是個非常奇怪的研究 , 因為宗教領袖們在做這些實驗時 , 只會用他們的文字來做這些實驗 , 因為宗教領袖們在做這些實驗時 , 只能找到任何東西 , 讓他們能找到任何東西 , 讓他們能找到任何東西 , 讓它變得更有趣 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	目前 , 基金會在這個領域的基礎研究上 , 以此為基礎的基礎研究 , 以此為基礎的基礎 , 來研究這個領域 , 以此為基礎的基礎研究 , 以此為基礎的基礎 , 以我們為基礎的基礎 , 來研究這個領域 , 以此為基礎的基礎 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	對於生物恐怖主義的威脅來說 , 它們是非常簡單的問題 , 可以用各種簡單的議題來製造清潔能源 , 也許革命化開發中國家能做什麼 , 並提供許多簡單的問題 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家哲學家菲利浦•薩維爾•帕茲維•辛巴爾曾說過:我們最初步的步驟 , 來改善我們的人生 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、心理學、心理學、心理學 。

life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是如此 , 反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性、反射性 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的熱情 , 會在那時刻的熱情下降 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少年的青少年年齡女孩 , 去婚姻謝謝你喬治 , 愛滋病 , 年齡的女孩們 , 將性愛情感染到婚姻中 , 直到婚姻謝謝你喬治 , 每年有60% , 愛滋病 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大多數人都沒有使用生氣控制 。
so much for promises .	為了承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們試試四歲的孩子 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	牠們可以有兩個 。 但如果他們等到實驗人員回來 , 他們就可以有兩個 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 若你喜歡馬鈴薯 , 等等 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	孩子們的兩分之二的孩子們給予教育 。

they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒了 , 反而是為了此而來的 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	我的同事在史丹佛大學回14年後 , 我同事在史丹佛大學的同事 , 試圖發現那些孩子的同事 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些抗拒絕對的孩子們 , 把250%的高度放在滿足 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很巨大 , 像是一整組不同的iq點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們不太麻煩 。 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自己自信的關鍵 , 而今天我所做的關鍵是 , 你的關鍵是 , 他們的關鍵是 , 不論你是誰 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 今天我要談的是什麼 ?
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	視覺是個人體驗的研究 , 分析你人類體驗到時間分裂、分裂的研究 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動化、無意識地 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化之間 , 在社會課堂之間 , 在社會課堂之間 , 彼此之間 , 社會課程之間 , 彼此之間的關係 , 來自於社會階級之間的關係 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 他們會變得很偏見 , 因為你學會會變得偏見 , 因為你學會讓其他人變得偏見 。
what determines any decision you make ?	決定你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做了一個決定 , 你要做一個決定 , 要做一個決定 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對於某些人而言 , 其他人正在做的事 , 以及你所感受的感覺 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 他們會稱之為 「 評論 」 , 因為他們的焦點就是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 重點是不好的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	一直在過去的情況下 , 我曾經經歷過什麼樣子 ?
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決策是根據過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會稱之為 「 過去 」 , 因為他們關注在哪裡 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 不是過去 , 而是未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點是關於預期的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們會稱之為 「 未來 」 , 他們的焦點是 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想要爭論的論點 , 每一決策劃中 , 你完全不知道 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	意思是 , 你有這些偏見的觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	這裡有兩種方法 , 有兩個方式可以分辨出來 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式是未來的 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在過去 , 或負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以稱之為 「 專注 」 、 「 生命 」 、 「 專注 」 、 「 生命 」 或 「 關注 」 的專注 , 不論你在人生中被控制 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以成為未來的目標 , 目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或你可以是獨立的未來:名字 , 生命開始死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出生態系統的需求 , 使得學會變得更好 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳的時刻是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度的高度在未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	現代的現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於消失和平面主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的結論是你從過去的原始點開始 , 你把你的家人、身份和你的家人、身份和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	未來的新挑戰 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的能量來探索自己 , 人們 , 能量 , 來探索自己、人、人、空間 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	每次觀點都比正面更有負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來的犧牲成功是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲了家庭時間 , 他們犧牲了家庭時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲了個人的成本 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了睡眠 , 所以它會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們生活在工作、成果和控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我確信在tedsterstersterstersterstersterstersterstersterstersterstersters 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 我是南布朗克斯的小小孩子 , 在南布朗克斯墨西哥灣 , 一個貧窮的孩子 , 在南布朗克斯的小小孩子 , 在南布朗克斯的小小孩子 , 一個貧窮的孩子 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我是一位未來的生長 , 讓我成為一個未來的機會 , 讓我成為一個未來的機會 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我 , 直到我學到平衡 , 直到我學到平衡 , 直到我學到平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加入了專注於過去 , 我比過去更有生產力、更有生產力、更有生產力、更有生產力 , 而且我比以前更有生產力 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們正在應用到許多世界問題:改變我們在學校的孩子們 , 和保育 , 改善良好的疾病 , 改善了許多世界問題:改變了我們在學校的孩子 , 和保育 , 和保育 , 改善良好的疾病 , 和保育 , 改善 , 和保育 , 和保育 , 改善了許多世界問題:改變了美國的孩子 , 和保育 , 改善了許多世界問題:改變 , 改善的家庭衝突 , 和保育 , 改善了許多世界問題 , 改善了許多世界問題:改變孩子們的死亡率 , 及保育 , 改善了許多世界問題 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以 , 最後 , 我想說:許多生命的謎題是透過理解你的觀點和其他人的謎題 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 但我認為後果很明顯 。

as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	直到2005年 , 世界各地地圖上有一百五百分之十五 , 一群在地圖上傳播的一群小說 , 谷歌的小說 , 谷歌的小說 , 谷歌的紅外線 , 和未知的路線 , 用在地圖上 , 讓人們在地圖上使用地圖 , 讓世界各地地圖地地圖 。

nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎金恩•諾貝爾獎得獎金恩•諾貝爾獎得獎金恩•諾貝爾獎金 , 讓大眾的關鍵在發展中國家的主要發展中國家是要把大量的大規模擴大 。

in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	去年 , 幾千名使用者在170個國家有數以千計的資料 , 並創造出一張地圖 , 以上千名的使用者 , 沒有想過 。

julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱利亞:注意到非暴力 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我一直在嘗試結束衝突與巴勒斯坦人 , 以色列與巴勒斯坦人 , 試圖終止衝突與巴勒斯坦人 , 試圖終止衝突與巴勒斯坦人 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國 , 一個問題總是出現在歐洲和美國 , 一個問題總是出現:在歐洲和美國 , 一個問題總是出現: 「 巴勒斯坦甘地嗎 ? 」
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼不是巴勒斯坦人使用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我常常聽到這問題時 , 我常常常常常常從中東 , 我從中東中東 , 我從中東 , 我從中東中東 , 我從中東來 , 用非暴力來防止他們的土地和水資源 , 用非暴力來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 來保護他們的土地和水資源 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者正在嘗試去建立和平在地區的大量國家非暴力運動 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大部分的人都可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	在地面和平的抗爭之下 , 這種分裂在地面上 , 和平的抗爭 , 是因為我們沒有和平的抗爭者 , 已經成功了 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我要講的是關於注意力的力量 , 關於注意力的力量 , 和你關注的力量 , 和你關注的力量 , 和你關注的力量 , 在西方銀行、加薩和其他地方 , 而非暴力運動的力量 , 就是你注意力的力量 , 你注意力的力量 , 和你關注的力量 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 對於非暴力的暴力來說 , 最不暴力的非暴力 , 而是為了我們開始對抗非暴力的暴力 , 而是為了我們開始對抗非暴力的暴力 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明一下這個村莊的村莊 , 叫做布魯斯 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為伊拉爾宣佈在村莊裡建造一個分裂的邊緣 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 所以他們會失去了40%的土地 , 所以他們會失去了40%的土地 , 所以他們會失去了40%的土地 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過啟發當地的領導者 , 他們發出了一個和平的抗議活動 , 他們發起了一個和平的抗議活動 , 讓它從事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短暫的影片 , 所以你有某種意義 , 讓你們看一些小小的看法 。

julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞:當我第一次聽到布魯斯的故事時 , 我很驚訝 , 在2003年 , 國際媒體失敗了 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是佛羅斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	長久以來 , 以色列與巴勒斯坦的民族群體之間 , 以色列與巴勒斯坦的民族團體 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦的角度來看 , 以色列與巴勒斯坦人之間的關係 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	巴勒斯坦的鄰居在西岸和巴勒斯坦的鄰居在西岸和巴勒斯坦的鄰居 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然在這些故事中很沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默的後果會發生在巴勒斯坦的後果 , 甚至生存 , 甚至生存 , 甚至生存 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力的抗爭 , 他們都是一個非常重要的共同點 , 他們都是一個共同點子的抗爭者 , 和非暴力抗爭者的共同點 , 他們都在共同點中分享一個重要的共同點 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力的領導者是唯一一個可靠的行動 , 讓國際注意到巴勒斯坦的議題 , 讓這個案例變得非常困難 , 非暴力的領導者 , 要讓他們在加入國際注意力的主題上 , 使他們成為一個難以置信的社會 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的注意力可能不會讓人驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓孩子長大的傷害 , 將他注意到第一次他把他的注意力降低 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	trum會成為童年心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 從孩子學到了 , 孩子們就知道他能得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以專注於孩子的行為 , 或將注意力放在他們的孩子身上 。
but that's true for adults too .	但這也是對成人的成年 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區的行為和國家都可以影響 , 依賴國際社群的行為 , 讓國際社會選擇關注關注 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在中東和平 , 將非暴力領袖在中東和平 , 將非暴力的領導者在中東和平 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在我的電影裡 , 加薩和東部的影片 , 加薩和東部的影片 , 我看到了影響力的影響 , 甚至一部紀錄片 , 甚至一部電影都能受到影響 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在村莊的村莊裡 , 社區和布魯斯的村莊非常相似 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被摧毀 , 失去了許多土地 , 失去了許多土地 , 失去了許多土地 , 失去了許多土地 , 沒有自由 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們從沒有人注意到兩年後 , 已經被關注了 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一個螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們告訴了最好的 , 被告知到達成危險 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 在電影中 , 人們在電影中看到的 , 那些人在電影裡 , 看到他們在電影中看到的 , 那些人在電影裡 , 感覺到 , 那些人都在做 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	右邊 , 有一個新和平運動 , 叫做slidariot , 它代表在伊斯蘭教堂上 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者已經使用了布德魯斯作為一個主要的領導者 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告 , 非暴力的力量 , 開始加入他們的行動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	華爾和蘇莉達的例子 , 可以扮演一個角色 , 讓非暴力成為一個角色 , 可以扮演角色的角色 , 讓非暴力轉變非暴力行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家們會變得更清楚 , 不暴力的示範 , 像是巴爾拉、阿拉、哈拉 , 和威爾拉•哈拉 , 和他們一起創作的力量 , 讓大眾媒體玩家們會變得更有力 , 不暴力的示範 , 會變得更有價值、和有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信 , 最重要的是要了解如果我們不願意注意到這些努力 , 它們是不可思議的 , 若我們不注意到這些努力 , 他們是不可思議的 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我看過第一手 , 如果我們這麼做 , 他們就會多次 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們多數 , 他們的影響會成長在巴勒斯坦衝突中 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響 , 可以終於無法阻止這種情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導者證明 , 非暴力在像布魯斯一樣 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給他們注意力 , 讓它們能證明它的運作方式 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	史蒂芬•蓋爾提出了一個簡單但強大的模型 , 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德、馬丁路德、馬丁路德 , 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德、馬丁......等等 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	商業、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家、企業家 ,
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙博士:偉大的領導者啟發了行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當我們假設時 , 不該怎麼解釋 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者 , 更好 , 你如何解釋其他東西能達成更好的事物 , 才能達成更好的假設 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	舉例來說 , 為什麼蘋果如此創新呢 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	一年後 , 他們比所有競爭更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的同性戀 , 同一個人 , 相同的同意 , 同一個同意 , 同一間的同意 , 同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那麼為什麼他們似乎有不同的樣子 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼是馬丁路德王國王國王國王國王國王國王國王權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一的美國人 , 他也不是唯一的美國人 , 而他肯定是不是唯一的美國人 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為何如此 , 權利的兄弟可以控制權力 , 控制權力 , 更好的資金 , 更好的資金 , 更好的資金 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成權力的兄弟 , 把他們帶到那邊 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前我發現了 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現徹底改變了我的觀點 , 甚至深深地改變了我的觀點 , 甚至徹底改變了我的觀點 , 甚至深深地改變了我的觀點 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 所有偉大、激勵的領導者和世界各地的領導者和組織 , 無論是蘋果 , 或馬丁•路德 , 或馬丁•路德 , 或馬丁•路德 , 或馬丁•路德 , 或馬丁•路德 , 或馬丁•路德金 , 他們都認為 , 行動和組織 , 都認為 , 行動和組織 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這是完全相反的 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的是 , 它可能是世界上最簡單的點子 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼辦 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小想法解釋為什麼一些組織和一些組織 , 有些領導者能夠啟發其他地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我非常快地說明一下 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 每個人 , 每個人 , 每個組織 , 都知道他們做什麼100% 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們如何做它 , 不論你稱之為 「 你的價值觀點 」 , 或你的使用 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但 , 很少人或組織知道為什麼他們會這麼做 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	為 「 為何 」 , 我不代表 「 為何 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 , 結果是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	為何 , 「 為何 ? 」 我是說:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上醒來 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為何有人在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果是 , 我們認為 , 我們的方式是從外面走出來的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 , 我們從最明顯的事物中發現了 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵的領導者和鼓舞的領導者 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我使用蘋果 , 因為他們很容易了解 , 每個人都得到 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果跟其他人一樣 , 市場的訊息是: 「 我們製作了很好的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們很漂亮設計 , 簡單使用和使用者友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一個嗎 ? 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這是最多的銷售方式 , 大部分的銷售方式是 , 大部分的人都在做 , 那就是我們溝通的多數 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們怎麼做 , 我們會說我們是怎麼做的 , 我們會說我們是怎麼樣的 , 我們會說 , 我們是怎麼樣的 , 像是這樣 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律師:我們有最好的律師 , 最好的律師 , 我們總是對我們的客戶做出商業 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的車子:它有很棒的氣體 , 可以買車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這是蘋果的溝通方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們都相信 , 我們在挑戰它 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信在思考不同 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰的是 , 使用者友善的方式 , 使用者友善的方式 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是要做好的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同嗎 ? 你準備好要買電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的是反映出這些資訊的資訊 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	告訴我們 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們不買你做什麼 , 買你做的事 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 , 他們買你做什麼 , 他們買你做的事 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋為什麼每個人在這個房間裡的每個人都很舒適 , 用蘋果電腦來買電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但是我們也很適用於蘋果電腦的蘋果 , 或蘋果電腦的蘋果 , 或蘋果的蘋果電腦 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如同我之前說過的 , 蘋果只是電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼 , 讓它們從任何地方都沒有 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者是所有這些產品的競爭 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們嘗試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 格雷特的電視節目 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們是很強大的 , 讓平方的電視節目 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們已經在製作螢幕的幾年了 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	das , 他們製造出很棒的產品 , 他們製造出很棒的產品 , 他們能製造出很棒的產品 , 他們能製造出很棒的產品 , 沒有人買了 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像購買一台飛行器 , 我們甚至無法想像買一台飛行器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會買一台電腦公司的一家公司 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 , 他們買你做什麼 , 他們買你做的事 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要做商業和所有人需要你所做的事 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要做那些相信你相信你相信的人 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	這是最好的部分:我告訴你們的是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	它是生物學的一部分 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你仔細觀察人類腦袋 , 你看到的是人類腦袋裡的一部分 , 看起來是人類的腦袋 , 結果是 , 你看到的是 , 人類的腦袋裡的三分之一 , 和黃金圈一樣 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的腦部 , 我們的腦部 , 我們的腦部 , 我們的腦部 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 和 「 什麼 」 的反應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮質是負責我們理性、分析想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間有兩個部分 , 我們的大腦負責了我們所有的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也對所有人類行為、決策、決策 , 都沒有能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們溝通到外面 , 人們可以了解很多複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、信息、信息、信息 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它只是不開動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能溝通時 , 大腦控制行為的一部分 , 我們會直接對大腦控制行為的一部分 , 讓人們能與我們溝通 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是槍枝的決定 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給別人所有事實和細節 , 說: 「 我知道這些事實和細節 , 只是沒有感覺 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會使用這種詞彙 , 不是 「 感覺 」 , 對吧 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦控制語言的一部分 , 控制決策並不控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的就是: 「 我不知道 , 沒有感覺好 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	有時候你會說你是你的心臟 , 或者你會帶著你的心靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭打破你 , 那些不是其他身體控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	大腦裡的所有東西都在你腦部的腦部 , 大腦控制決策和非語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你要做什麼 , 你會怎麼做 , 要做你做的事 , 讓人們對你做些什麼 , 或更重要的是 , 更重要的是 , 更重要的是 , 要為你做些什麼 , 並且想要成為你所做的 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再次 , 目標不只是要賣給那些你相信你相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標並不只需要工作 , 而是僱用你相信你所相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我常常說 , 如果你雇用你的人 , 他們會工作 , 因為他們能做工作 , 他們會工作 , 因為他們能做工作 , 如果你僱用你的人 , 你就知道 , 如果你雇用你的人 , 他們會用血液、汗和淚 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	另外還有一個更好的例子 , 比如同一個更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大多數人都不知道samuelpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	在20世紀初期 , 權力飛行器的追求力量是天空的力量 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試它 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierpontlangley , 我們假設是成功的成功 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的公司失敗了 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的三件事 , 不論是錯誤的 , 壞市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總共有三件事情 , 所以讓我們來探險 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpontlangley有五萬美金 , 讓五萬美金 , 讓這台機器飛行 。
money was no problem .	錢不是問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在史密森尼亞和史密森尼亞的大海上 , 他知道所有偉大的心智 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的心智能找到和市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報追蹤他 , 每個人都在各地走路 , 每個人都在找尋他 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 我們從來沒有聽過阿姆uelpontlangley呢 ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里 , 在華盛頓特區 , 他們沒有我們認為是成功的成功 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 給他們的夢想 , 和紐約時報一樣 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差異是 , 阿爾布爾堡 , 是由一個目標所驅動的 , 由於一個目標 , 由一個目的 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能找出這個飛機機器 , 它將會改變世界 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要是富有的 , 他想要是富有的 , 他想要成為富裕的 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求財富 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信 , 人們相信 , 愛德華兄弟的夢想是用血液、汗和青少年來 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只為了付錢 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說 , 每次當作者都要拿五個零件時 , 他們會需要花五個部分 , 因為那是有多少時候 , 他們會要花五個部分 , 因為那是他們要花五個部分的原因 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在12月17日 , 11月17日 , 在12月17日 , 在12月17日 , 沒有人能經歷它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更明顯的 , 雷射出了錯誤的原因:天氣 , 飛機 , 飛機飛機 , 他就飛行了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 這是一個驚人的發現 , 我會改善你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有很有錢 , 他沒有很有錢 , 他沒有很有錢 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 , 他們買你做什麼 , 他們買你做的事 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你相信你相信的人 , 你會吸引那些相信你相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你相信的人 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	叫做 「 創新 」 的法律 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你肯定知道 「 法律 」 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們的第一百分之一是創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13% , 我們的人口是早期的成員 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你最早期的主要和你的階段 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	唯一的原因就是因為你不能買電子手機 。

how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你如何記得你在哪裡 ? 你如何記得你在哪裡 ? 你如何記得你的車子 , 你如何記得你在哪裡 ? 神經科學學家神經科學學家神經科學學家尼爾•蓋爾的神經科學家 , 神經科學學家的神經科學學家 , 神經科學學家的神經科學家們都在對記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、科學、探索、探索、神經科學 。

and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家們開始了解 , 藉由個人神經元的神經元 , 藉由個人的神經元 , 或探索一個環境來尋找食物 。

so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到的是 , 神經元知道 , 當老鼠進入一個特定的地方時 , 這種神經元就知道了 。

so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們能顯示出神經元的功能是動物的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元 , 我們就會看到不同的神經元 , 我們會看到不同的神經元 , 我們會看到不同的神經元 , 像是在這個平方的藍色區域 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們在我的環境中 , 與大腦聯繫在一起 , 說: 「 我現在在哪裡 ? 」

it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	它就像你記得在哪個地方 , 哪個地方的細胞 , 可以從哪個角落到地位 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方的模式 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方的模式 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方的模式 。

so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們能把這些路徑往往往往往後 , 我們就知道 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們可以在這個路上走路 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 我們可以在這個路上走路 , 以往往往往往方向回來 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	細胞也將這種細胞稱為 「 網絡細胞 」 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	相反地 , 細胞會發現 , 像細胞一樣 , 它們就像地方細胞一樣 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但現在 , 每個個體細胞 , 每個個體細胞都在一個非常普遍的環境中 , 每個個體細胞都在一個非常普遍的環境中 , 每個個體都在一個不同的位置上 , 以一個不同的位置 , 以一種非常普遍的角度來看待 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從數量的圖案轉移到其他細胞中 , 每個細胞都在不同顏色的圖案中 , 每個細胞都有一種特色的圖案 , 每個細胞都跟其他細胞相同 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以 , 紅色的紅色則是這個紅色的紅色 , 上面的紅色 , 上面的紅色 , 上面的紅色 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 用三角形 , 像你在地圖上找到的地圖 , 用三角形的角度來看 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電動力可以透過這些細胞來追蹤它 , 所以它可以用它的動力來追蹤它 , 所以它可以用它的動力來追蹤它的動力 , 讓它可以用它的動力來追蹤它 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有幹細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有的圖像都有相同的神經元素 , 它意味著 , 神經細胞的特定位置 , 它意味著 , 神經細胞的特定位置在哪個方向 , 或跑步 , 這意味著 , 我們對稱的 「 神經細胞 」 的特定位置 , 它意味著 「 網絡 」 的特定位置 , 意味著我們在哪個方向上移動 , 或跑步在六個方向之間 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人們放在mri掃描儀中 , 把他們放在mri掃描儀中 , 把他們放在mri掃描儀中 , 讓大家看這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	實際上 , 你可以看到它在人類皮層的大腦中 , 你可以看到它是大腦的一部分 , 你可以看到它是大腦的一部分 。
so back to homer .	回到家裡 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能記得他的車是位於距離和方向的位置 , 讓他停車在哪裡 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這會被稱為 「 無線電池 」 的標準 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也記得他從車輛公園的路徑 , 會被稱為 「 網絡 」 的路徑 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以讓細胞變成細胞 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到那個地方的位置 , 讓他在他的腦袋裡找到最好的圖案 , 把他的車子放在他的腦袋裡 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這會引導他回到那個地點 , 像是他的車子在哪裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	或許它已經被禁止了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道 , 他知道哪裡 , 所以他知道它是哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除此之外 , 我們看到在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 例如 , 只要我們在整個大腦中看到它 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是神經機制 , 使我們想要想像它們 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這個情況發生了 , 你的記憶可以從一個細胞開始 , 讓細胞在你周圍周圍的空間結構上 , 來創造出周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	格細胞可以透過這個空間來移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 如同我所說的 , 沒有提到的 , 它們會像個細胞一樣 , 我沒有提到 , 你正在面對的 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你的視覺影像 , 你可以想像發生在這個圖片中 , 你可以想像發生在哪裡 , 你可以想像發生什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新時代的神經元 , 我們開始了解心理學過程 , 像是你記得 , 或甚至認為在數十億個個人神經元的神經元中 , 我們開始了解心理過程 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 一個全球安全的機制 , 政府、私人部門、政府、私人部門、政府、私人部門、政府、私人部門、政府、私人部門、政府、私人部門 , 和公眾 , 不只不過是詹姆斯•史蒂斯 , 不只不過是詹姆斯•史蒂斯 , 不只不過是詹姆斯•史蒂斯 , 不只不過是詹姆斯•史蒂斯 , 來解釋為什麼安全的未來 , 會被合作 , 和公共場所 , 不只會被合作 , 和公共場所 , 不只不過是未來應該要和公共場所所做的 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、社群媒體、政策、政治、社群媒體、暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史蒂夫:美國總統的主題是關於全球安全的主題 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談的是開放的安全性 , 因為我們必須在21世紀開始更安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我開始說 , 咱們來看看20世紀 , 對於我們來說 , 安全的運作方式是怎樣的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是在法國北部的北部 , 在法國的北部 , 法國的軍隊在法國北部 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在1916年 , 在1916年 , 大約有2000萬人被殺死了 , 大約有2000萬人被殺死了 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你將它轉移到20世紀的安全 , 第二次世界大戰 , 你看到了兩百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們繼續嘗試建造牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們走進冷戰戰爭中 , 第二次世界大戰結束時 , 我們進入冷戰戰場 , 然後我們進入冷戰戰場 , 然後進入冷戰 , 第二次世界大戰 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	今天我對我們所說的 , 不是建造橋樑 , 而是建立橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是來自伊斯蘭教堂的一部分 , 和巴勒斯坦河流行的一部分 , 談到 , 關於如何 , 它在歐洲和巴爾斯的大樓上有很大的橋樑 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 一起開始 , 開始 , 一起合作 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我認為 , 再次 , 開放式的共通點 , 開放原始的公共空間 , 和社交網路有關聯繫國際關係 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我來談一下為什麼我們需要這樣做 , 因為我們的全球常見被建造牆壁 , 不必要做這件事 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我是很明顯的 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一艘船 , 橫跨印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張圖片是什麼樣子 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它會在那邊的邊緣 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	這是為了避免鳥類攻擊 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	現今的威脅是全球的威脅 , 這是印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	piracy也在馬拉克加上非常活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它在大腸道上游泳 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海裡看到它 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	這是全球運輸系統的10億美元 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 500個火星人有了20個海盜 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是全球常見的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉移到不同的海洋 , 網海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	那時 , 他們被監禁 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們在10億美金上得到了信用卡片 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟的一部分 。
two trillion a year .	兩兆美元 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是在英國的gdp上 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以這個網際網路 , 我們所知無限的基礎設備是很大的基礎設備 , 基本上是極端的基礎設備 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	另一件事我擔心的是威脅來自阿富汗 , 來自阿富汗 , 來自阿富汗 , 來自阿富汗 , 從阿富汗到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心古柯鹼來自北方的古柯鹼 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心人類販賣的武器和販賣 , 除非法武器和販賣 , 或許我們擔心人類販賣 , 和販賣 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	交易在海裡的其他部分是全球常見的一部分 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我可以告訴各位 , 這是一張非常高的技術 , 我們要用它來阻止垃圾 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一種可靠藥品的銷售 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它在南美洲的叢林裡建造 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們把它帶著六噸的硬幣 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個非常複雜的溝通方式 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種交易、武器、武器、武器、武器、武器、武器、武器、武器的一部分 , 是威脅到全球共同的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	咱們來看看阿富汗的阿富汗 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的場景 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	8%到90% , 來自阿富汗 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	我們也看到了 , 當然恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是alqaeda所做的 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的急迫性 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	這恐怖主義是全球共同的一部分 , 我們必須加入 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 我們是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道20世紀的工具無法運作 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我會說 , 我們不會把安全性從槍枝的角度來看 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會從槍枝的角度來看待安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要使用軍隊的力量 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這麼做時 , 我們必須做它 , 我們必須做得很好 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的聯繫是國際網路 , 開放式的關聯網絡 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我給你們幾個例子 , 說明它如何運作的方式 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 , 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都是書籍 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這有點奇怪 , 我以為我讀到這張圖片 , 三十歲的年輕人 , 和女性在阿富汗 。 」
you would be correct .	你會正確 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	85%無法閱讀當他們進入安全軍隊的安全力量 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班和婦女學會學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以 , 問題是 , 為什麼他們都站著書籍 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們正在教導他們閱讀書籍 , 與私人的合作夥伴合作 , 合作夥伴與私人機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教導了超過200萬個阿富汗的安全力量 , 來閱讀並寫下一個基本層面 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你閱讀和寫在阿富汗時 , 你通常會把筆放在你的口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在這些年輕男人和女人畢業時 , 他們把這筆錢放進口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這裡有50個國家參與這個任務 , 將國際聯繫在一起 , 將國際聯繫起來 , 將國際聯繫起來 , 將國際聯繫起來 , 將國際聯繫起來 , 將國際聯繫起來 , 將國際聯繫起來 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	現在 , 我們也教導這些技巧 , 當然 , 但我會說 , 開放式的安全感 , 能讓它更長時間安全 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國軍隊的戰爭 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做 「 舒適 」 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一個姐妹的船叫做 「 隱私 」 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院船 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這種事 , 加勒比亞和南美洲的合作 , 會造成病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在典型的cruise , 他們會40萬個病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它不是被軍隊的結合 , 而是透過軍隊的組合 , 讓人道主義組織的結合: 「 合作 」 、 「 計畫微笑 」 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織會寄給志願者 。
interagency physicians come out .	內部醫師們來了 。
they're all part of this .	他們都是這樣 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 8歲的孩子 , 8歲 , 和他的母親兩天來到眼睛診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他站起來時 , 他突然看著 , 說: 「 mamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamamama
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽媽 , 我看到世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	透過400萬個病人治療 , 你開始看到創造安全力的力量 , 非常不同的方式 。
